Hellboy(2004) ★★★ Ron Perlman, Jo

“150 criminals locked up in Nottingham in 2019”

Time Line

Man jailed for having a craft knife at a food bank A man was jailed for 148 days after being caught with a craft knife at a food bank. Mark Rose, of Ilkeston Road, Nottingham, visited Grace Church Nottingham at the Ministry in Castle Boulevard with a friend at 11am on October 28. Officers said he was waiting outside when he was approached by a member of security staff, who said she had been told he was carrying a knife. He denied having a weapon on him but, when searched, had the craft knife in his jacket pocket. The 39-year-old was arrested on suspicion of possession of a bladed article. He admitted the offence and was sentenced at Nottingham Crown Court on Friday, December 20. PC Charles Willett, who led the investigation, said: “While Rose did not take the knife out of his pocket, it is still an offence to carry a knife in public. “This case should act as a warning to anyone thinking of carrying weapons that we will seek to put them before the court if we catch them in possession of weapons, regardless of whether they are used.”

Life with a minimum of 10 years for man who tried to kill his wife in their bed A pizza delivery man was handed a life sentence for stabbing his wife and leaving her with 25 wounds. Habibullah Faizi went downstairs to collect two knives for the attack as she lay in bed at their home in Newquay Avenue, Bobbers Mill. At his trial in Nottingham Crown Court, a jury heard that his victim’s life was only saved by the intervention of neighbours and emergency medical care on January 2. Faizi, 40, denied attempted murder but was found guilty. The case had been adjourned after the conflicting views of two psychiatrists. Judge John Burgess imposed a life term with a minimum period of custody of 10 years. But the Parole Board will have to be satisfied that Faizi is safe to be freed and he could remain in prison indefinitely. The judge believed Faizi was suffering from a mental disorder at the time but that his attack left his wife with “serious long-term physical and psychological harm.” The judge said: “The paramedics counted 25 wounds before they had to stop counting. She had a fractured skull, punctured lung and perforated bowel. “You attacked with such force that one of the knives broke, leaving fragments embedded in the scalp. To fracture the skull and break the knife would have required severe force.” Faizi told the court he has no memory of stabbing his wife. Rachel Darby, defending, said that the attack was “spontaneous” and that he was ill at the time with some “psychotic symptoms.” But she said this did not add up to a defence to the charge. He had never been in trouble before. Miss Darby said: “There was no physical violence towards his wife or any other persons.” The judge ordered him never to contact her again.

Jailed for life A teenager was jailed for life for the gang murder of former Arnold schoolboy Jaden Moodie. Jaden - who had studied at Redhill Academy - became the year’s youngest gang victim when he was knocked off a scooter and stabbed nine times in Leyton, east London, on January 8. The killing was caught on graphic CCTV footage, which was shown in the Old Bailey trial of Ayoub Majdouline, 19. The teenage drug dealer was one of five Mali Boy gang members who had set out in a stolen Mercedes into rival Beaumont Crew territory. Majdouline, who had been identified as a “modern slavery” victim, had admitted drug dealing for the Mali Boys but denied being involved in 14-year-old Jaden’s murder. But jurors heard his DNA was found on a bloody yellow rubber glove and knife discarded after the killing. At the Old Bailey, he was found guilty of Jaden’s murder and having a blade. Judge Richard Marks QC sentenced him to life in prison with a minimum term of 21 years plus 18 months to run concurrently. Judge Marks said Jaden had been associated with the rival Beaumont Crew gang, but “he did not deserve to die”.

More than 15 years in prison A 41-year-old man who attacked a woman with a dumbbell, stick and metal pole was jailed for 15 years and six months. Mounaim Elfidh, of Gilbert Road, in Bircotes was sentenced on Tuesday, December 17, after being found guilty by a jury at Nottingham Crown Court of three counts of section 18 wounding, unlawful imprisonment and production of cannabis. The incident happened on May 9 this year where Elfidh assaulted a woman with a stick, causing serious injuries to her head and legs. The attack continued which led to the weapon snapping in half due to the force of the attack. A dumbbell was also thrown at the woman’s shoulder, and he further assaulted her with a metal pole. The woman was also punched. The victim tried to escape the property, but Elfidh locked the doors so she couldn’t leave. Later that afternoon, she managed to leave and contacted the police. He was arrested the next day. The victim attended hospital and was treated for a head injury. She also had visible bruising across a large area of her body.

Brexiteer Amy Dalla Mura jailed for harassing Anna Soubry Left, Amy Dalla Mura and right, former MP Anna Soubry A Brexiteer who repeatedly harrassed former MP Anna Soubry was jailed for 28 days. Amy Dalla Mura, 56, was also banned from the Broxtowe constituency in the run up to the general election where she had been standing against Ms Soubry. Dalla Mura appeared in Westminister Magistrates’ Court on Monday, December 16, where the court heard how she had targeted Ms Soubry between January and March this year, turning up at events and calling her a “traitor” on live television. Former MP Ms Soubry, a Remainer who lost her Broxtowe seat while standing for the Independent Group for Change, said she was left “frightened” following the incidents. Dalla Mura, of Eton Villas, Hove, claimed that her behaviour was politically motivated debate and did not accept it was frightening, despite standing in the General Election in the same constituency as Ms Soubry. Dalla Mura, who denied harassment but was found guilty following a trial at Westminster Magistrates’ Court, is banned from contacting Ms Soubry under a three-year restraining order.

Woman stole perfume from Debenhams A shoplifter blamed an illicit cigarette for landing her back in jail after stealing again following six days of freedom. Lynette Burton’s solicitor told a court that it played a part in leaving her homeless and getting back into trouble. Rory Macmillan, mitigating, told Nottingham Magistrates’ Court: “She reported to probation again and to the council three days in a row, trying to get somewhere to live. “They would not give her anywhere, because on a previous occasion, they put her in a hotel. She was caught smoking a cigarette against regulations and so she was left with nowhere to live. “She has been homeless since being released. “She managed to sort out some benefits to come but in the intervening time she shoplifts,” added Mr Macmillan. Burton, 36, admitted stealing four Lancome perfumes valued at £297 from Debenhams on Long Row on October 31; and theft of perfumes worth £276 from the same shop on December 13. She was sent to prison for 20 weeks. This will not increase her time inside because she will now have to serve the rest of a one-year term, after being released at the halfway point. District Judge Leo Pyle told her: “It is a sad state of affairs that on being released, you embark upon this latest spree.” Daniel Pietryka, prosecuting, said that Burton was stopped when leaving the Long Row shop on October 31. The perfumes were seized but she escaped with them earlier this month. She must pay Debenham’s compensation of £276. When asked for her address in court, Burton said she had no home, but could be contacted through a property on St Matthias Road, which is in St Ann’s.

Burglar with ‘horrendous record’ jailed after stealing TV from student flats A burglar was jailed for four years for taking a £40 TV from student flats. Imran Khan, 43, was filmed walking down the street with the television across his shoulders, a court heard. He claimed to have just bought it from a man who was taking it to a pawn shop - but a jury unanimously found him guilty of burglary. Recorder Ben Gumpert QC said that Khan had so many burglary offences on his record that he was liable to least three years in prison. Sitting at Nottingham Crown Court, he told Khan: “You told transparent lies which the jury found to be precisely that. “You were aware you were going to receive a sentence of more than three years if you were convicted. “In the context of domestic burglary, no violence was used and no threats were used. Nevertheless, the offence is aggravated by your previous convictions.” The recorder said that Khan had a “horrendous record.” Jonathon Dee, prosecuting, said that the television was recovered after being taken from the house on Lenton Boulevard on June 28.

Long Eaton man who attacked his mum three times found hiding in her wardrobe Betts slapped and kicked his own mother previously (Image: Derbyshire Constabulary) A Long Eaton man was found hiding in his mum’s wardrobe after breaking a restraining order that was put in place for attacking her three times. Marc Betts, 47, of Northcote Street in Long Eaton, pleaded guilty to breaching his restraining order at Southern Derbyshire Magistrates’ Court. Betts had just come out of prison when he breached the order - which had been put in place until October 24, 2022, according to Derbyshire Live. Lynn Bickley, prosecuting, said: “On December 12 at five to four in the afternoon police received a report that the defendant was at the cottages by a neighbour. “When officers arrived they are allowed into the address by the mother and the defendant was found hiding in a wardrobe. “He was arrested and interviewed by police, and answered no comment.” Nick Wenden, mitigating, said: “This is clearly a breach of the restraining order, and his previous convictions list is not pleasant.” “He bumped into his mother and he had not seen her since. “She invited him to the address. He does know he should not have gone. “But he was desperate after just having come from prison and he wanted to try and make amends.” District judge Jonathan Taaffe handed Betts a 26-week jail term. He also ordered him to pay a £122 victim surcharge.

Fraudster applied for credit card by stealing couple’s details from letterbox Ephraim Chivunga, left, and Tondarai Murungu, right A fraudster who used a rogue credit card to pay for a room at a Nottinghamshire hotel enjoyed his stay so much he posted it on Facebook, a court heard. Asylum seeker Ephraim Chivunga had booked two rooms for four people - but was using a card fraudulently applied for by co-accused Tondarai Murungu, who is also seeking asylum. Abi Joyce, prosecuting, said the pair went around Nottinghamshire and Lincolnshire carrying out offences with the credit card and a stolen fuel card. Details to apply for the card, which was used to pay at the hotel, had been stolen from a couple’s letterbox. They returned home in 2016 to a letter telling them their Debenhams master card was over the limit of £4,000. “They had never taken out a Debenhams master card,” explained Miss Joyce. Police gathered CCTV stills of Murungu and a white van loitering at their address. Both defendants admitted handling a stolen fuel card - which had been a replacement card that was never received by the owner. Murungu, 39, of Bathley Street, The Meadows, was jailed for two years for fraud and handling stolen goods. Murungu said there was a third party, who was the main player, putting together the original idea. He got ten percent from the £4,000 spent on the card. Chivunga, 38, of Silverdale Road, Basford, was jailed for a total of 33 months for fraud, handling the stolen fuel card, possessing an article for fraud - fake Marks and Spencer vouchers - and frauds relating to false Boots and WH Smith vouchers.

Dangerous driver reached 140mph on M1 in dramatic police chase A drug dealer was jailed after he reached speeds of up to 140mph along the M1 during a police chase. Mohammed Khan was locked up for seven years for a catalogue of drugs offences and dangerous driving. He was behind the wheel of a BMW when he overtook an officer in a police car as he joined the M1, at junction 29 at Chesterfield, on November 15 this year. Khan was pulled over at junction 30. But as the officer got out to speak with him, Khan sped off - driving back onto the M1 southbound and reaching 140mph at one stage. The 39-year-old slowed to 80mph at junction 29 and entered an area as if he was going to leave the motorway. Alan Murphy, prosecuting at Nottingham Crown Court, said: “He darted back onto the motorway, through the hatched area, before commencement of the slip road. “He went back up to 130mph at Tibshelf. He narrowly missed a car moving from lane four to three”. Police laid a stinger at the next junction which Khan went over before driving through a red light. He tried to drive on but could not because he had flat tyres. He ran off but was soon caught. Ecstasy, cocaine and cannabis, for personal use, were found in a bag near the car. More ecstasy was found at his home address in Hadfield Close, Sheffield. Paperwork was also found linking him to a Nottingham address. Khan also faced sentence for more drugs offences. Police saw a Lexus in Bathley Street, The Meadows, with the driver appearing to be slumped in the seat on May 3, 2018. They stopped the car in Crocus Street and detained Khan. Four boxes of “business cards” were discovered in the boot, which Mr Murphy told the court were “plainly a drug dealer’s card”. They had a mobile number on them and the words “strictly no texts!” and “around 11am till late”, plus the letters “AB” - indicating the Class of drugs sold and the time sales were available. A search of the car turned up drugs in a void behind the driver’s door panel and the door - which could only be opened with a multi-tool. Judge Stuart Rafferty QC gave Khan concurrent sentences of 15 months for dangerous driving, four years each for possessing cocaine and Ecstasy with intent to supply, and no separate penalty for possessing cannabis. For the 2018 offences, he received concurrent sentences of three years each for possessing cocaine and Ecstasy with intent to supply, two years for possessing cannabis with intent to supply and two years for selling cannabis. The three years was consecutive to the four years. He was banned from driving for four-and-a-half years and must take an extended retest.

Fraudster jailed A man who caused “serious distress and financial hardship” to his employer was jailed after he swindled more than £128,000 from the business. Adam Cartwright, 39, of Hazel Hill Crescent in Bestwood Park, started working for B&M Installations in 2011 as an electrician and it was there he began to buy electrical parts the company did not use. The company, which is based just outside Carrington in Pelham Street, began investigating in October 2018 after a project manager became aware of an invoice containing higher costs than expected for a project they were working on. Upon the discovery, Nottinghamshire Police’s fraud team began looking into Cartwright’s business dealings and found him to be buying extra electrical parts across 50 separate invoices. The parts came to a total of just over £128,000. Cartwright pleaded guilty to fraud by abuse of position at Nottingham Crown Court on Tuesday, December 19. He was subsequently sentenced to two years and eight months in jail. Detective constable Jason Jenkins, of Nottinghamshire Police, said: “Fraud can have a devastating impact on businesses and it was clear from the outset that Cartwright’s actions caused serious distress to the business owners, as well as financial hardship. “The sentence clearly demonstrates that we take fraud offences incredibly seriously and will deal with those responsible.”

Burglar jailed A burglar took goods set aside for charity when he cycled past an unlocked shed. But Michael Smedley was spotted by a neighbour who had helped sort out the DIY goods for the British Heart Foundation, a court heard. Tom Heath, prosecuting, told Nottingham Crown Court: “Police arrived and Mr Smedley was still inside the shed. He said the door was open.” When Smedley was searched, officers found a can of “CS incapacitant spray” in one of his pockets. He claimed he thought it was paint, said Mr Heath. The court heard the offence took place on July 22, three months after he had been given a one-year suspended jail sentence. He had 55 crimes on his record. A one-year prison term was ordered for Smedley, 44, of Beacon Drive, Kirkby-in-Ashfield, who admitted shed burglary and having a CS spray. Recorder Justin Widoger told him: “You saw the shed was unlocked and decided to help yourself. “The items were going to be donated to a charity for the general good. You didn’t know that.” Digby Johnson, mitigating, described the offence as “opportunistic.” He said Smedley suffers from chronic obstructive pulmonary disease as well as thrombosis in the legs. He had been due to have an ultra-sound scan at the Queen’s Medical Centre. Smedley knew he was at risk of custody but the suspended sentence had been imposed for an affray, a different type of offence, said Mr Johnson.
